<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#ddd"><span style="font-weight:normal;">  <span class="reflink plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:ComparePages&amp;rev1=477164519&amp;page2=Alprazolam">(verify)</a></span></span></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Alprazolam</b>, available under the trade name <b>Xanax</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Potency_(pharmacology)" title="Potency (pharmacology)">potent</a>, short-acting <a href="/wiki/Anxiolytic" title="Anxiolytic">anxiolytic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> <a href="/wiki/Chemical_classification" title="Chemical classification">class</a>. It is commonly used for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a>, especially of <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorder</a>, but also in the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Generalized_anxiety_disorder" title="Generalized anxiety disorder">generalized anxiety disorder</a> (GAD) or <a href="/wiki/Social_anxiety_disorder" title="Social anxiety disorder">social anxiety disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APAguide_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-APAguide-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup> It was the 12th most prescribed medicine in the United States in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Alprazolam, like other benzodiazepines, binds to specific sites on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GABAA" title="GABAA">GABA<sub>A</sub></a> <a href="/wiki/Receptor_(biochemistry)" title="Receptor (biochemistry)">receptor</a>. It possesses <a href="/wiki/Anxiolytic" title="Anxiolytic">anxiolytic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hypnotic" title="Hypnotic">hypnotic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skeletal_muscle_relaxant" title="Skeletal muscle relaxant">skeletal muscle relaxant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anticonvulsant" title="Anticonvulsant">anticonvulsant</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amnestic" title="Amnestic">amnestic</a> properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mandrioli_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-mandrioli-7">[7]</a></sup> Alprazolam is available for <a href="/wiki/Oral_administration" title="Oral administration">oral administration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tablet_(pharmacy)" title="Tablet (pharmacy)">compressed tablet</a> (CT) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extended-release" title="Extended-release">extended-release</a> <a href="/wiki/Capsule_(pharmacy)" title="Capsule (pharmacy)">capsule</a> (XR) formulations.</p>
<p>Peak benefits achieved for <a href="/wiki/Generalized_anxiety_disorder" title="Generalized anxiety disorder">generalized anxiety disorder</a> (GAD) may take up to a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verster2004_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verster2004-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Drug_tolerance" title="Drug tolerance">Tolerance</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Anxiolytic" title="Anxiolytic">anxiolytic</a>/antipanic effects is controversial with some authoritative sources reporting the development of tolerance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22391278_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22391278-10">[10]</a></sup> and others reporting no development of tolerance;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APAguide_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-APAguide-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pav10_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pav10-11">[11]</a></sup> tolerance will, however, develop to the <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a>-<a href="/wiki/Hypnotic" title="Hypnotic">hypnotic</a> effects within a couple of days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pav10_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pav10-11">[11]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Withdrawal_symptoms" title="Withdrawal symptoms">Withdrawal symptoms</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebound_symptoms" title="Rebound symptoms">rebound symptoms</a> may occur after ceasing treatment abruptly following a few weeks or longer of steady dosing, and may necessitate a gradual dose reduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verster2004_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Verster2004-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APPT_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-APPT-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam was first released by <a href="/wiki/Upjohn" title="Upjohn">Upjohn</a> (now a part of <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>) in 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The first approved use was panic disorder and within two years of its original marketing Xanax became a blockbuster drug in the US. Presently, alprazolam is the most prescribed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-14">[14]</a></sup> and the most misused <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn2neodredv_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-dawn2neodredv-15">[15]</a></sup> The potential for misuse among those taking it for medical reasons is controversial with some expert reviews stating that the risk is low and similar to that of other benzodiazepine drugs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APAguide_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-APAguide-4">[4]</a></sup> and others stating that there is a substantial risk of misuse and dependence in both patients and non-medical users of alprazolam and that the pharmacological properties of alprazolam, high affinity binding, high potency, having a short <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elimination_half-life" title="Elimination half-life">elimination half-life</a> as well as a rapid onset of action may increase the misuse potential of alprazolam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22391278_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22391278-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-16">[16]</a></sup> Compared to the large number of prescriptions, relatively few individuals increase their dose on their own initiative or engage in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug-seeking_behavior" title="Drug-seeking behavior">drug-seeking behavior</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DEAbrief_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-DEAbrief-17">[17]</a></sup> Alprazolam is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schedule_IV_(US)" title="Schedule IV (US)">schedule IV</a> controlled substance by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a> (DEA).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_uses">Medical uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Medical uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alprazolam is mostly used to treat <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nausea" title="Nausea">nausea</a> due to <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">chemotherapy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-16">[16]</a></sup> The FDA label advises that the physician should periodically reassess the usefulness of the drug.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup> Alprazolam may also be indicated for the treatment of generalized anxiety disorder, as well as for the treatment of anxiety conditions with co-morbid depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Alprazolam is also often prescribed with instances of <a href="/wiki/Hypersomnia" title="Hypersomnia">hypersomnia</a> and co-morbid sleep deficits.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panic_disorder">Panic disorder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Panic disorder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alprazolam is effective in the relief of moderate to severe <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panic_attacks" title="Panic attacks">panic attacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup> However, it is not a first line treatment since the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitors" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitors">selective serotonin reuptake inhibitors</a>, and alprazolam is no longer recommended in Australia for the treatment of panic disorder due to concerns regarding tolerance, dependence and abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22391278_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22391278-10">[10]</a></sup> Evidence supporting the effectiveness of alprazolam in treating panic disorder has been limited to 4 to 10 weeks. However, people with panic disorder have been treated on an open basis for up to 8 months without apparent loss of benefit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xcppdmm_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-xcppdmm-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, alprazolam is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration_(United_States)" title="Food and Drug Administration (United States)">FDA-approved</a> for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorder</a> with or without <a href="/wiki/Agoraphobia" title="Agoraphobia">agoraphobia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup> Alprazolam is recommended by the World Federation of Societies of Biological Psychiatry (WFSBP) for treatment-resistant cases of panic disorder where there is no history of <a href="/wiki/Drug_tolerance" title="Drug tolerance">tolerance</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_dependence" title="Drug dependence">dependence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anxiety_disorders">Anxiety disorders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Anxiety disorders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anxiety associated with depression is responsive to alprazolam. Demonstrations of the effectiveness by systematic clinical study are limited to 4 months duration for anxiety disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-fdalabel082011-5">[5]</a></sup> However, the research into antidepressant properties of alprazolam is of poor quality and only assessed the short-term effects of alprazolam against depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_Marwijk-2012_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-van_Marwijk-2012-21">[21]</a></sup> In one study, some long term, high-dosage users of alprazolam developed reversible depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In the US, alprazolam is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration_(United_States)" title="Food and Drug Administration (United States)">FDA-approved</a> for the management of anxiety disorders (a condition corresponding most closely to the APA <i>Diagnostic and Statistical Manual</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DSM-IV-TR" title="DSM-IV-TR">DSM-IV-TR</a> diagnosis of generalized anxiety disorder) or the short-term relief of symptoms of anxiety. In the UK, alprazolam is recommended for the short-term treatment (2–4 weeks) of severe acute anxiety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xcppdmm_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-xcppdmm-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bnf_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-bnf-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nausea_due_to_chemotherapy">Nausea due to chemotherapy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Nausea due to chemotherapy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alprazolam may be used in combination with other medications for <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy-induced_nausea_and_vomiting" title="Chemotherapy-induced nausea and vomiting">chemotherapy-induced nausea and vomiting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pregnancy_and_lactation">Pregnancy and lactation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pregnancy and lactation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Benzodiazepines cross the placenta, enter the fetus and are also excreted with breast milk. The use of benzodiazepines during pregnancy or <a href="/wiki/Lactation" title="Lactation">lactation</a> has potential risks. The use of alprazolam in pregnancy is believed to be associated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congenital_abnormalities" title="Congenital abnormalities">congenital abnormalities</a>.</p>
<p>Women who are pregnant or are planning on becoming pregnant should avoid starting alprazolam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Use in the last trimester may cause fetal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_dependence" title="Drug dependence">drug dependence</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Withdrawal_symptoms" title="Withdrawal symptoms">withdrawal symptoms</a> in the post-natal period<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> as well as neonatal flaccidity and respiratory problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> However, in long-term users of benzodiazepines abrupt discontinuation due to concerns of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teratogenesis" title="Teratogenesis">teratogenesis</a> has a high risk of causing extreme withdrawal symptoms and a severe <a href="/wiki/Rebound_effect" title="Rebound effect">rebound effect</a> of the underlying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_health_disorder" title="Mental health disorder">mental health disorder</a>. Spontaneous abortions may also result from abrupt withdrawal of psychotropic medications including benzodiazepines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benzodiazepines, including alprazolam, are known to be excreted in human milk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Chronic administration of diazepam, another benzodiazepine, to nursing mothers has been reported to cause their infants to become lethargic and to lose weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aoxsemuadi_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-aoxsemuadi-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contraindications">Contraindications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Contraindications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Benzodiazepines require special precaution if used in children and in alcohol- or drug-dependent individuals. Particular care should be taken in pregnant or elderly patients, patients with substance abuse history, particularly alcohol dependence and patients with comorbid psychiatric disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Use of alprazolam should be avoided or carefully monitored by medical professionals in individuals with the following conditions: <a href="/wiki/Myasthenia_gravis" title="Myasthenia gravis">myasthenia gravis</a>, acute narrow-angle <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">glaucoma</a>, severe liver deficiencies (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Cirrhosis" title="Cirrhosis">cirrhosis</a>), severe <a href="/wiki/Sleep_apnea" title="Sleep apnea">sleep apnea</a>, pre-existing respiratory depression, marked neuromuscular respiratory weakness including unstable <a href="/wiki/Myasthenia_gravis" title="Myasthenia gravis">myasthenia gravis</a>, acute <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulmonary" title="Pulmonary">pulmonary</a> insufficiency, chronic <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychosis</a>, hypersensitivity or <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">allergy</a> to alprazolam or other drugs in the <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> class, <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a> (may induce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicidality" title="Suicidality">suicidality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Episodic_dyscontrol_syndrome" title="Episodic dyscontrol syndrome">dyscontrol</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bnf_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-bnf-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hori_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-hori-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like all <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depressants" title="Depressants">depressants</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">alcohol</a>, alprazolam in larger-than-normal doses can cause significant deterioration in <a href="/wiki/Alertness" title="Alertness">alertness</a>, combined with increased feelings of drowsiness, especially in those unaccustomed to the drug's effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> People driving or conducting activities that require vigilance should exercise caution in using alprazolam or any other depressant until they know how it affects them.</p>
<p>Elderly individuals should be cautious in the use of alprazolam due to the possibility of increased susceptibility to side-effects, especially loss of coordination and drowsiness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aoxsemuadi_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-aoxsemuadi-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverse_effects">Adverse effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Adverse effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xanax_2_mg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1477" data-file-width="997" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Xanax_2_mg.jpg/220px-Xanax_2_mg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Xanax_2_mg.jpg/330px-Xanax_2_mg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Xanax_2_mg.jpg/440px-Xanax_2_mg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xanax_2_mg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Xanax (alprazolam) 2 mg tri-score tablets</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Allergic reactions are unlikely to occur. The only common side effect is sleepiness when treatment is initiated.</p>
<p>Possible side effects include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Disinhibition" title="Disinhibition">Disinhibition</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaundice" title="Jaundice">Jaundice</a> (very rare)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hallucination" title="Hallucination">Hallucinations</a> (rare)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xerostomia" title="Xerostomia">Dry mouth</a> (infrequent)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ataxia" title="Ataxia">Ataxia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slurred_speech" title="Slurred speech">slurred speech</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suicidal_ideation" title="Suicidal ideation">Suicidal ideation</a> (rare)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hori_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-hori-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Urinary_retention" title="Urinary retention">Urinary retention</a> (infrequent)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ase_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ase-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skin_rash" title="Skin rash">Skin rash</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_depression" title="Respiratory depression">respiratory depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constipation" title="Constipation">constipation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drftb_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-drftb-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acmirttoadom_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-acmirttoadom-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anterograde_amnesia" title="Anterograde amnesia">Anterograde amnesia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barbee95_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barbee95-45">[45]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Attention" title="Attention">concentration</a> problems</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Somnolence" title="Somnolence">Drowsiness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dizziness" title="Dizziness">dizziness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lightheadedness" title="Lightheadedness">lightheadedness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(medical)" title="Fatigue (medical)">fatigue</a>, unsteadiness and impaired <a href="/wiki/Motor_coordination" title="Motor coordination">coordination</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertigo_(medical)" title="Vertigo (medical)">vertigo</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drftb_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-drftb-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acmirttoadom_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-acmirttoadom-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paradoxical_reactions">Paradoxical reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Paradoxical reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1138" data-file-width="1525" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg/220px-Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg/330px-Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg/440px-Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Side_effects_of_alprazolam.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Side_effect" title="Side effect">Side effects</a> from alprazolam</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although unusual, the following <a href="/wiki/Paradoxical_reaction" title="Paradoxical reaction">paradoxical reactions</a> have been shown to occur:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aggression" title="Aggression">Aggression</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rage_(emotion)" title="Rage (emotion)">Rage</a>, hostility<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fasciculations" title="Fasciculations">Twitches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tremor" title="Tremor">tremor</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mania" title="Mania">Mania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychomotor_agitation" title="Psychomotor agitation">agitation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperactivity" title="Hyperactivity">hyperactivity</a> and restlessness<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drug_interactions">Food and drug interactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Food and drug interactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alprazolam is primarily metabolised via <a href="/wiki/CYP3A4" title="CYP3A4">CYP3A4</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otani-2003_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Otani-2003-51">[51]</a></sup> Combining <a href="/wiki/CYP3A4" title="CYP3A4">CYP3A4</a> inhibitors such as <a href="/wiki/Cimetidine" title="Cimetidine">cimetidine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erythromycin" title="Erythromycin">erythromycin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfluoxetine" title="Norfluoxetine">norfluoxetine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluvoxamine" title="Fluvoxamine">fluvoxamine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itraconazole" title="Itraconazole">itraconazole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ketoconazole" title="Ketoconazole">ketoconazole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nefazodone" title="Nefazodone">nefazodone</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propoxyphene" title="Propoxyphene">propoxyphene</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ritonavir" title="Ritonavir">ritonavir</a> delay the hepatic clearance of alprazolam, which may result in excessive accumulation of alprazolam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> This may result in exacerbation of its adverse effect profile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cpoati_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-cpoati-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Imipramine" title="Imipramine">Imipramine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desipramine" title="Desipramine">desipramine</a> have been reported to be increased an average of 31% and 20%, respectively, by the <a href="/wiki/Concomitant_drug" title="Concomitant drug">concomitant</a> administration of alprazolam tablets in doses up to 4 mg/day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Combined oral contraceptive pill">Combined oral contraceptive pills</a> reduce the clearance of alprazolam, which may lead to increased plasma levels of alprazolam and accumulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">Alcohol</a> is one of the most important and common interactions. Alcohol and benzodiazepines such as alprazolam taken in combination have a synergistic effect on one another, which can cause severe sedation, behavioral changes, and intoxication. The more alcohol and alprazolam taken the worse the interaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Michel_L.2C_Lang_JP_2003_479.E2.80.9385-36">[36]</a></sup> Combination of alprazolam with the herb <a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">kava</a> can result in the development of a semi-comatose state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hypericum" title="Hypericum">Hypericum</a> conversely can lower the plasma levels of alprazolam and reduce its therapeutic effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overdose">Overdose</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overdose">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xanax_0.25,_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="701" data-file-width="1006" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg/220px-Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg/330px-Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg/440px-Xanax_0.25%2C_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xanax_0.25,_0.5_%26_1_mg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Xanax 0.25, 0.5 and 1 mg scored tablets</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_overdose" title="Benzodiazepine overdose">Benzodiazepine overdose</a></div>
<p>Overdoses of alprazolam can be mild to severe depending on how much of the drug is taken and any other drugs that have been taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam overdoses cause excess <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> (CNS) depression and may include one or more of the following symptoms:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ase_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-ase-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Somnolence" title="Somnolence">Somnolence</a> (drowsiness)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hypotension" title="Hypotension">Hypotension</a> (low blood pressure)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthostatic_hypotension" title="Orthostatic hypotension">Orthostatic hypotension</a> (fainting while standing up too quickly)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hypoventilation" title="Hypoventilation">Hypoventilation</a> (shallow breathing)</li>
<li>Impaired motor functions
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dizziness" title="Dizziness">Dizziness</a></li>
<li>Impaired balance</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Muscle_weakness" title="Muscle weakness">Muscle weakness</a></li>
<li>Impaired or absent reflexes</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fainting" title="Fainting">Fainting</a></li>
<li>Coma and death are possible if alprazolam is combined with other substances.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dependence_and_withdrawal">Dependence and withdrawal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dependence and withdrawal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_dependence" title="Benzodiazepine dependence">Benzodiazepine dependence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_withdrawal_syndrome" title="Benzodiazepine withdrawal syndrome">Benzodiazepine withdrawal syndrome</a></div>
<p>Alprazolam, like other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benzodiazepines" title="Benzodiazepines">benzodiazepines</a>, binds to specific sites on the GABA<sub>A</sub> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma-amino-butyric_acid" title="Gamma-amino-butyric acid">gamma-amino-butyric acid</a> receptor. When bound to these sites, which are referred to as benzodiazepine receptors, it modulates the effect of GABA A receptors and, thus, GABAergic neurons. Long-term use causes adaptive changes in the benzodiazepine receptors, making them less sensitive to stimulation and less powerful in their effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stahl_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stahl-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Drug_withdrawal" title="Drug withdrawal">Withdrawal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebound_symptoms" title="Rebound symptoms">rebound symptoms</a> commonly occur and necessitate a gradual reduction in dosage to minimize withdrawal effects when discontinuing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verster2004_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Verster2004-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not all withdrawal effects are evidence of true dependence or withdrawal. Recurrence of symptoms such as anxiety may simply indicate that the drug was having its expected anti-anxiety effect and that, in the absence of the drug, the symptom has returned to pretreatment levels. If the symptoms are more severe or frequent, the patient may be experiencing a <a href="/wiki/Rebound_effect" title="Rebound effect">rebound effect</a> due to the removal of the drug. Either of these can occur without the patient's actually being drug-dependent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stahl_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stahl-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam and other benzodiazepines may also cause the development of <a href="/wiki/Physical_dependence" title="Physical dependence">physical dependence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug_tolerance" title="Drug tolerance">tolerance</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_withdrawal_symptoms" title="Benzodiazepine withdrawal symptoms">benzodiazepine withdrawal symptoms</a> during rapid dose reduction or cessation of therapy after long-term treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> There is a higher chance of withdrawal reactions if the drug is administered in a higher dosage than recommended, or if a patient stops taking the medication altogether without slowly allowing the body to adjust to a lower-dosage regimen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashton_manual_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ashton_manual-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1992, Romach and colleagues reported that dose escalation is not a characteristic of long-term alprazolam users, and that the majority of long-term alprazolam users change their initial pattern of regular use to one of symptom control only when required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some common symptoms of alprazolam discontinuation include malaise, weakness, insomnia, tachycardia, lightheadedness, and dizziness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Patients taking a dosing regimen larger than 4 mg per day have an increased potential for dependence. This medication may cause withdrawal symptoms upon abrupt withdrawal or rapid tapering, which in some cases have been known to cause seizures. The discontinuation of this medication may also cause a reaction called <i>rebound anxiety</i>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Delirium" title="Delirium">Delirium</a> similar to that produced by the tropane alkaloids (gaba antagonists) of Datura (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyoscine_hydrobromide" title="Hyoscine hydrobromide">scopolamine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atropine" title="Atropine">atropine</a>) and seizures have been reported in the medical literature from abrupt alprazolam discontinuation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 1983 study of patients who had taken long-acting benzodiazepines, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Clorazepate" title="Clorazepate">clorazepate</a>, for extended periods, the medications were stopped abruptly. Only 5% of patients who had been taking the drug for less than 8 months demonstrated withdrawal symptoms, but 43% of those who had been taking them for more than 8 months did. With alprazolam – a short-acting benzodiazepine – taken for 8 weeks, 65% of patients experienced significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebound_anxiety" title="Rebound anxiety">rebound anxiety</a>. To some degree, these older benzodiazepines are self-tapering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schatzberg_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schatzberg-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The benzodiazepines <a href="/wiki/Diazepam" title="Diazepam">diazepam</a> (Valium) and <a href="/wiki/Oxazepam" title="Oxazepam">oxazepam</a> (Serepax) have been found to produce fewer withdrawal reactions than alprazolam (Xanax), <a href="/wiki/Temazepam" title="Temazepam">temazepam</a> (Restoril/Normison), or <a href="/wiki/Lorazepam" title="Lorazepam">lorazepam</a> (Temesta/Ativan). Factors that determine the risk of <a href="/wiki/Substance_dependence" title="Substance dependence">psychological dependence</a> or <a href="/wiki/Physical_dependence" title="Physical dependence">physical dependence</a> and the severity of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_withdrawal_symptoms" title="Benzodiazepine withdrawal symptoms">benzodiazepine withdrawal symptoms</a> experienced during dose reduction of alprazolam include: dosage used, length of use, frequency of dosing, personality characteristics of the individual, previous use of cross-dependent/cross-tolerant drugs (alcohol or other sedative-hypnotic drugs), current use of cross-dependent/-tolerant drugs, use of other short-acting, high-potency benzodiazepines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid1686752_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid1686752-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and method of discontinuation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashton_manual_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ashton_manual-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Detection_in_body_fluids">Detection in body fluids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Detection in body fluids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alprazolam may be quantitated in blood or plasma to confirm a diagnosis of poisoning in hospitalized patients, provide evidence in an impaired driving arrest or to assist in a medicolegal death investigation. Blood or plasma alprazolam concentrations are usually in a range of 10–100 μg/L in persons receiving the drug therapeutically, 100–300 μg/L in those arrested for impaired driving and 300–2000 μg/L in victims of acute overdosage. Most commercial immunoassays for the benzodiazepine class of drugs will cross-react with alprazolam, but confirmation and quantitation is usually performed using chromatographic techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacology">Pharmacology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pharmacology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alprazolam is classed as a high-potency benzodiazepine and is a triazolobenzodiazepine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> namely a benzodiazepine with a <a href="/wiki/1,2,3-Triazole" title="1,2,3-Triazole">triazole ring</a> attached to its structure. As a benzodiazepine, alprazolam produces a variety of therapeutic and adverse effects by binding to the benzodiazepine receptor site on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GABA_A_receptor" title="GABA A receptor">GABA<sub>A</sub></a> receptor and modulating the function of the <a href="/wiki/GABA_receptor" title="GABA receptor">GABA receptor</a>, the most prolific inhibitory receptor within the brain. The GABA chemical and receptor system mediates inhibitory or calming effects of alprazolam on the nervous system. The GABA<sub>A</sub> receptor is made up of 5 subunits out of a possible 19, and GABA<sub>A</sub> receptors made up of different combinations of subunits, have different properties, different locations within the brain, and, importantly, different activities with regard to benzodiazepines. Alprazolam and other triazolobenzodiazepines like <a href="/wiki/Triazolam" title="Triazolam">triazolam</a> have that have a triazol ring attached to their structure appear to have <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressant</a> properties since this type of structure with these three rings is similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Tricyclic_antidepressant" title="Tricyclic antidepressant">tricyclic antidepressants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barbee95_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barbee95-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Benzodiazepines and in particular alprazolam causes a marked suppression of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypothalamicpituitary-adrenal_axis" title="Hypothalamicpituitary-adrenal axis">hypothalamicpituitary-adrenal axis</a>. The therapeutic properties of alprazolam are similar to other benzodiazepines and include <a href="/wiki/Anxiolytic" title="Anxiolytic">anxiolytic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anticonvulsant" title="Anticonvulsant">anticonvulsant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscle_relaxant" title="Muscle relaxant">muscle relaxant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hypnotic" title="Hypnotic">hypnotic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Amnesia" title="Amnesia">amnesic</a>, however it is used mainly as an anxiolytic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mandrioli_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-mandrioli-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Administration of alprazolam compared <a href="/wiki/Lorazepam" title="Lorazepam">lorazepam</a>, has been demonstrated to elicit a statistically significant increase in extracellular <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">dopamine</a> <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_receptor_D1" title="Dopamine receptor D1">D1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_receptor_D2" title="Dopamine receptor D2">D2</a> concentrations in the <a href="/wiki/Striatum" title="Striatum">striatum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacokinetics">Pharmacokinetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pharmacokinetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Absorption</b></p>
<p>Following oral administration, alprazolam is readily absorbed. Peak concentrations in the plasma occur in one to two hours following administration. Plasma levels are proportionate to the dose given; over the dose range of 0.5 to 3.0 mg, peak levels of 8.0 to 37 ng/mL were observed. Using a specific assay methodology, the mean plasma elimination half-life of alprazolam has been found to be about 11.2 hours (range: 6.3 to 26.9 hours) in healthy adults.</p>
<p><b>Distribution</b></p>
<p>In vitro, alprazolam is bound (80 percent) to human serum protein. Serum albumin accounts for the majority of the binding.</p>
<p><b>Metabolism/Elimination</b></p>
<p>Alprazolam is extensively metabolized in humans, primarily by cytochrome P450 3A4 (Cyp3A4), to two major metabolites in plasma: 4-hydroxyalprazolam and α- hydroxyalprazolam. A benzophenone derived from alprazolam is also found in humans. Half-lives are similar to that of alprazolam. The plasma concentrations of 4-hydroxyalprazolam and α-hydroxyalprazolam relative to unchanged alprazolam concentration were always less than 4%. The reported relative potencies in benzodiazepines receptor binding experiments and in animals models of induced seizure inhibition are 0.2 and 0.66, respectively, for 4-hydroxyalprazolam and α-hydroxyalprazolam. Such low concentrations and lesser potencies of 4-hydroxyalprazolam and α-hydroxyalprazolam suggest that they are unlikely to contribute much to the pharmacological effects of alprazolam. The benzophenone metabolite is essentially inactive.</p>
<p>Alprazolam and its metabolites are excreted primarily in the urine.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Forms_of_alprazolam">Forms of alprazolam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Forms of alprazolam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alprazolam regular release and orally disintegrating tablets are available as 0.25 mg, 0.5 mg, 1 mg, 2 mg strength tablets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam extended release tablets are available as 0.5 mg, 1 mg, 2 mg, and 3 mg strength tablets.</p>
<p>Alprazolam oral solutions are available as 0.5 mg/5 mL and as 1 mg/1 mL oral solutions.</p>
<ul>
<li>Active ingredient: alprazolam</li>
<li>Inactive ingredients: microcrystalline cellulose, corn starch, docusate sodium, povidone, sodium starch glycollate, lactose monohydrate, magnesium stearate, colloidal silicon dioxide and sodium benzoate. In addition, the 0.25 mg tablet contains D&amp;C Yellow No. 10 and the 0.5 mg tablet contains FD&amp;C Yellow No. 6 and D&amp;C Yellow No. 10</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patent">Patent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Patent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is covered under <span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US3987052" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 3,987,052</a></span>, which was filed on 29 October 1969, granted on 19 October 1976, and expired in September 1993.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational_use">Recreational use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Recreational use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_misuse" title="Benzodiazepine misuse">Benzodiazepine misuse</a></div>
<p>There is a risk of misuse and dependence in both patients and non-medical users of alprazolam; the pharmacological properties of alprazolam such as high affinity binding, high potency, being short-acting and having a rapid onset of action increase the abuse potential of alprazolam. The physical dependence and withdrawal syndrome of alprazolam also adds to the addictive nature of alprazolam. In the small subgroup of individuals who escalate their doses there is usually a history of alcohol or other substance use disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22391278_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22391278-10">[10]</a></sup> Despite this, most prescribed alprazolam users do not use their medication recreationally, and the long-term use of benzodiazepines does not generally correlate with the need for dose escalation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> However, based on US findings from the Treatment Episode Data Set (TEDS), an annual compilation of patient characteristics in substance abuse treatment facilities in the United States, admissions due to "primary tranquilizer" (including, but not limited to, benzodiazepine-type) drug use increased 79% from 1992 to 2002, suggesting that misuse of benzodiazepines may be on the rise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> also reported in 2011 that "The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention last year reported an 89 percent increase in emergency room visits nationwide related to nonmedical benzodiazepine use between 2004 and 2008."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam is one of the most commonly prescribed and misused benzodiazepines in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APPT_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-APPT-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn2neodredv_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-dawn2neodredv-15">[15]</a></sup> A large-scale nationwide U.S. government study conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAMHSA" title="SAMHSA">SAMHSA</a> found that, in the U.S., benzodiazepines are recreationally the most frequently used pharmaceuticals due to their widespread availability, accounting for 35% of all drug-related visits to hospital emergency and urgent care facilities. Men and women are equally likely to use benzodiazepines recreationally. The report found that alprazolam is the most common benzodiazepine for recreational use followed by <a href="/wiki/Clonazepam" title="Clonazepam">clonazepam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorazepam" title="Lorazepam">lorazepam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diazepam" title="Diazepam">diazepam</a>. The number of emergency room visits due to benzodiazepines increased by 36% between 2004 and 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn2neodredv_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-dawn2neodredv-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Regarding the significant increases detected, it is worthwhile to consider that the number of pharmaceuticals dispensed for legitimate therapeutic uses may be increasing over time, and DAWN estimates are not adjusted to take such increases into account. Nor do DAWN estimates take into account the increases in the population or in ED use between 2004 and 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn2neodredv_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-dawn2neodredv-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>At a particularly high risk for misuse and dependence are people with a history of alcoholism or drug abuse and/or dependence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and people with <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alprazolam, along with other benzodiazepines, is often used with other recreational drugs. These uses include aids to relieve the panic or distress of <a href="/wiki/Dysphoria" title="Dysphoria">dysphoric</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Bad_trip" title="Bad trip">bad trip</a>") reactions to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychedelic_drugs" title="Psychedelic drugs">psychedelic drugs</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LSD" title="LSD">LSD</a>, and the drug-induced <a href="/wiki/Psychomotor_agitation" title="Psychomotor agitation">agitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a> in the "<a href="/wiki/Comedown_(drugs)" title="Comedown (drugs)">comedown</a>" stages of <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulant</a> use, such as <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phencyclidine" title="Phencyclidine">phencyclidine</a> allowing sleep. Alprazolam may also be used in conjunction with other <a href="/wiki/Depressant" title="Depressant">depressant drugs</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Opioid" title="Opioid">opioids</a>, in an attempt to enhance the psychological effect of these drugs. Alprazolam may be used in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>, with users citing a synergistic effect achieved after consuming the combination.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poly-drug_use" title="Poly-drug use">poly-drug use</a> of powerful depressant drugs poses the highest level of health concerns due to a significant increase in the likelihood of experiencing an <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">overdose</a> which may result in fatal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_depression" title="Respiratory depression">respiratory depression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 1990 study claimed that diazepam has a higher misuse potential relative to other benzodiazepines, and that some data suggests that alprazolam and lorazepam resemble diazepam in this respect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid1981067_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid1981067-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anecdotally injection of alprazolam has been reported, causing dangerous damage to blood vessels, closure of blood vessels (embolization) and decay of muscle tissue (<a href="/wiki/Rhabdomyolysis" title="Rhabdomyolysis">rhabdomyolysis</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Alprazolam is practically not soluble in water, when crushed in water it will not fully <a href="/wiki/Solubility" title="Solubility">dissolve</a> (40 µg/ml of <a href="/wiki/Properties_of_water" title="Properties of water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a> at pH 7).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DB00404_Alprazolam_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-DB00404_Alprazolam-95">[95]</a></sup> There have also been anecdotal reports of alprazolam being <a href="/wiki/Insufflation_(medicine)" title="Insufflation (medicine)">snorted</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Due to the low weight of a dose, alprazolam in one case was found to be distributed on blotter paper in a manner similar to LSD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Slang terms for alprazolam vary from place to place. Some of the more common terms are shortened versions of the trade name "Xanax", such as Bars or Xannies (or Xanies);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> references to their drug classes, such as benzos or downers; or remark upon their shape or color (most commonly a straight, perforated tablet or an oval-shaped pill): bars, Z-bars, footballs, planks, poles, blues, or blue footballs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Availability">Availability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Availability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alprazolam is available in English-speaking countries under the following brand names:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Alprax, Alprocontin, Alzam, Alzolam, Anzilum, Apo-Alpraz, Kalma, Mylan-Alprazolam, Niravam, Novo-Alprazol, Nu-Alpraz, Pacyl, Restyl, Tranax, Trika, Xycalm, Xanax, Xanor, Zolam, Zopax, Helex.</li>
</ul>
<p>As of December 2013, in anticipation of the rescheduling of alprazolam to Schedule 8 in Australia—Pfizer Australia announced they would be discontinuing the Xanax brand in Australia as it is no longer commercially viable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alprazolam has varied legal status depending on jurisdiction:</p>
<ul>
<li>In the United States, alprazolam is a prescription drug and is assigned to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schedule_IV_(US)" title="Schedule IV (US)">Schedule IV</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Controlled_Substances_Act" title="Controlled Substances Act">Controlled Substances Act</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>Under the UK drug misuse classification system benzodiazepines are class C drugs (Schedule 4).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Note that in the UK, alprazolam is not available on the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a> and can only be obtained on a private prescription.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BNF60_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-BNF60-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li>In Ireland, alprazolam is a Schedule 4 medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, alprazolam is a prescription drug in List IV (Schedule 4) under the Narcotics Drugs Act (1968).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, alprazolam is a List 2 substance of the <a href="/wiki/Opium_Law" title="Opium Law">Opium Law</a> and is available for prescription.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, alprazolam was originally a Schedule 4 (Prescription Only) medication; however, as of February 2014, it has become a Schedule 8 medication, subjecting it to more rigorous prescribing requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Internationally, alprazolam is included under the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Psychotropic_Substances" title="Convention on Psychotropic Substances">Convention on Psychotropic Substances</a> as Schedule IV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alprazolam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-fdalabel082011-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fdalabel082011_5-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2011/018276s045lbl.pdf" rel="nofollow">"FDA approved labeling for Xanax revision 08/23/2011"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. Federal Drug Administration. 2011-08-23. p. 4<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2011-09-14</span></span>. <q>Anxiety Disorders – XANAX Tablets (alprazolam) are indicated for the management of anxiety disorder (a condition corresponding most closely to the APA Diagnostic and Statistical Manual [DSMIII-R] diagnosis of generalized anxiety disorder) or the short-term relief of symptoms of anxiety. Anxiety or tension associated with the stress of everyday life usually does not require treatment with an anxiolytic... Panic Disorder – XANAX is also indicated for the treatment of panic disorder, with or without agoraphobia... Demonstrations of the effectiveness of XANAX by systematic clinical study are limited to 4 months duration for anxiety disorder and 4 to 10 weeks duration for panic disorder; however, patients with panic disorder have been treated on an open basis without any apparent loss of benefit. The physician should periodically reassess the usefulness of the drug for the individual patient.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAlprazolam&amp;rft.btitle=FDA+approved+labeling+for+Xanax+revision+08%2F23%2F2011&amp;rft.date=2011-08-23&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.accessdata.fda.gov%2Fdrugsatfda_docs%2Flabel%2F2011%2F018276s045lbl.pdf&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.pub=Federal+Drug+Administration&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
